  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8b6ff0ee-f624-4347-ba9d-90b3c94086d5'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer1732473876892084878">Before WICKED was formed, before the Glade was built, before Thomas entered the Maze, sun flares hit the earth and mankind fell to disease.<br/><br/>Mark and Trina were there when it happened, and they survived. But surviving the sun flares was easy compared to what came next. Now a disease of rage and lunacy races across the eastern United States, and there’s something suspicious a</span>
  <span id="freeText1732473876892084878" style="display:none">Before WICKED was formed, before the Glade was built, before Thomas entered the Maze, sun flares hit the earth and mankind fell to disease.<br /><br />Mark and Trina were there when it happened, and they survived. But surviving the sun flares was easy compared to what came next. Now a disease of rage and lunacy races across the eastern United States, and there’s something suspicious about its origin. Worse yet, it’s mutating, and all evidence suggests that it will bring humanity to its knees.<br /><br />Mark and Trina are convinced there’s a way to save those left living from descending into madness. And they’re determined to find it—if they can stay alive. Because in this new, devastated world, every life has a price. And to some, you’re worth more dead than alive.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1732473876892084878" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/127746-does-this-installment-shed-any-light-on">Does this installment shed any light on books one and two? I thought the first book was okay, but number two was really atrocious. Thinking maybe 0.5 will help me understand number 2? And no, I haven&#39;t read three yet because two was just so bad...</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_127746'><a id="like_count_community_question_127746" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/127746?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">7 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F13089710-the-kill-order">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/127746-does-this-installment-shed-any-light-on">6 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/127746-does-this-installment-shed-any-light-on">See all 7 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/8921530-sasha"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1363121783i/8921530.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/8921530-sasha">Sasha</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">If you found book 2 atrocious, book 3 won't be any better. I thought 0.5 a bit too spoiler-y if you are going to read it before 3. The new characters <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">If you found book 2 atrocious, book 3 won't be any better. I thought 0.5 a bit too spoiler-y if you are going to read it before 3. The new characters are not any more imaginative than the ones we already have and you can draw clear parallels between them and the ones from books 1-3 (especially the main characters Mark and Trina -&gt; Thomas and Teresa). If I hadn't purchased book 3 and 0.5 together with book 2, I definitely would've stopped. <br /><br />When you read the prequel it just shows again that the world of the Maze Runner just sort of spiraled out of proportion, like the author was trying to find a reason behind everything that happened in first book. It just didn't add up, made no sense whatsoever and well...I did not like it. It's not to say that there weren't good parts to it: It's fast paced and creepy and has you reading the whole thing in no time, but my problem was really the reason behind it all and the characters that just had no depth whatsoever. <br /><br />My comment comes a bit late so maybe you have already had the chance to read it and make up your mind. Either way, I hope if you did get to read it, that your disappointment wasn't as big as mine. <br /><br />-Sasha <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_247203398" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/247203398" />
    <a title="Aneeqah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5357469-aneeqah"><img alt="Aneeqah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1304355209p2/5357469.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/247203398?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aneeqah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aneeqah" href="/user/show/5357469-aneeqah">Aneeqah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5357469-aneeqah?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5357469-aneeqah?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5357469-aneeqah?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5357469-aneeqah?shelf=review-for-blog">review-for-blog</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5357469-aneeqah?shelf=the-reading-games">the-reading-games</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5357469-aneeqah?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5357469-aneeqah?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer247203398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14123545015983452771">I can describe this book to you in a single word: disappointment. With a big capital D. See, the thing is, The Maze Runner was one of my favorite series ever… until the last book, which I hated. So the only reason I picked this book up was in hope that it would redeem the series for me and answer my bajillion questions. Unfortunately, that didn’t happen. The Kill Order just failed to live up to The Maze Runner.<br/><br/>I think the thing that bothered me the most about this book was that it was not about </span>
  <span id="freeText14123545015983452771" style="display:none">I can describe this book to you in a single word: disappointment. With a big capital D. See, the thing is, The Maze Runner was one of my favorite series ever… until the last book, which I hated. So the only reason I picked this book up was in hope that it would redeem the series for me and answer my bajillion questions. Unfortunately, that didn’t happen. The Kill Order just failed to live up to The Maze Runner.<br /><br />I think the thing that bothered me the most about this book was that it was not about Thomas and the rest of the Gladers. You would think that it would be, right? That’s what I was hoping for. Instead, this book is about some random people that I’m not 100% sure are connected to Thomas or anyone else. And because we don’t know anything about this set of characters, we’re left with even more questions. Sure, a few of my questions about the world building and all that were answered in this book, but I just ended up with so many more questions about everything in the series and specifically this book that will never be answered now.<br /><br />The Kill Order along with having a new set of characters, had a ton of action. Non stop action, actually. If you know me, you’ll know that I love action in books. But even me, the teenager who loves action, thought that there was just. too. much. On every page, there was something going on, and I’m going to be honest… I got bored. I lost interest in the book, because nothing else was going on besides the action. Sure, action is fantabulous, but there’s a limit to how much you can have in a single book<br /><br />Overall, I just could not bring myself to enjoy The Kill Order, even though I enjoyed the first two books of the series so much. We were left with a bajillion more questions, and there was way too much action for me to even remotely enjoy this book. If you don’t mind either of those two things, then you should give this book a shot, otherwise, I would pass this one up if I were you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14123545015983452771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6038711544068699375"><u>[Conversation in the editing room]</u><br/><br/>Remember all of the semi-likeable characters from the original series? <i>
  <b>Get rid of them</b>

  <b> Double them</b>
</i><br/><br/>Should we give it a decent ending? <b>
  <i>*ominous silence*</i>
</b><br/><br/><b>Annnnd....that's about it</b><br/><br/>We are set far before the first novel - in the heart of the <b>initial Sun Flares and virus outbreak. </b> We get front-row seats to the start of the apocalypse. <br/><br/>There's a <b> whole new expendable cast</b> that provides quite convenient</span>
  <span id="freeText6038711544068699375" style="display:none"><u>[Conversation in the editing room]</u><br /><br />Remember all of the semi-likeable characters from the original series? <i>
  <b>Get rid of them</b>
</i><br /><br />How about all the plot-holes from the first three books? <i>
  <b> Double them</b>
</i><br /><br />Should we give it a decent ending? <b>
  <i>*ominous silence*</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>Annnnd....that's about it</b><br /><br />We are set far before the first novel - in the heart of the <b>initial Sun Flares and virus outbreak. </b> We get front-row seats to the start of the apocalypse. <br /><br />There's a <b> whole new expendable cast</b> that provides quite convenient fodder and a <b> enough plot holes to bury all of them.</b><br /><br />The pacing of this book really threw me for a loop.<br /><br /> Every second of the book was spent in <b><u>heart</u>-<u>pumping</u> <u>action</u>.</b> Literally, all we did was<b> race from plot arc to plot arc</b> without taking time for character development or anything decent to happen.<br /><br />And when things finally did calm down, <b>Dashner only upped the tension</b> by having everyone shout their plans and ideas. And the arguments...it was all 'science person wants to do this' and 'stupid army guy wants to do this' and 'civilian is running around with his head cut off'<b>...the usual.</b><br /><br /><b>AND THAT SO-CALLED-SCIENCE</b> - oooo, that reallllly rustled my jimmies. I can't even. The science. Ugh. Incoherent rage.<br /><br />But seriously, when you are going to go for a science-based explanation for your series...you think it would begin by <b>being rooted in...science. </b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Honestly. What was the author thinking.</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br />Read by Mark Deakins and he did an okay job. It just felt a bit bland overall. <div id="review_1079689022" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1079689022" />
    <a title="Dylan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7716112-dylan"><img alt="Dylan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489066831p2/7716112.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1079689022?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dylan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dylan" href="/user/show/7716112-dylan">Dylan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780385742894" href="/book/show/17797357-the-kill-order">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7716112-dylan?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7716112-dylan?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1079689022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16667155642633942594">My first ever 1 star review. Well done 'The Kill Order', you deserve it. <br/><br/><b>Before Reading it</b><br/>-Oh I hope this is good!<br/><br/><b>During and After reading it</b><br/><p>

<div id="review_358315125" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/358315125" />
    <a title="B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5206717-b"><img alt="B" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/358315125?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="B" href="/user/show/5206717-b">B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Those who don't need character development along with their action</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=netgalley-edelweiss-arc">netgalley-edelweiss-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=didn-t-see-that-coming">didn-t-see-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=i-totally-saw-that-coming">i-totally-saw-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=judge-a-book-by-the-cover">judge-a-book-by-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=read-reviewed">read-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer358315125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14415262172325415113">Actual Rating: 3.5 stars<br/><br/>There are the books that either have too little action and you're bored to tears reading said book, or book that have too much action, and too little of everything else. <i>The Kill Order</i> tends to fall in the latter category of books, and I'll bet that was where Dashner was intending <i>The Kill Order</i> to fall. <br/><br/>The plot for <i>The Kill Order</i> is simple - it's the end of the world, sun flares are destroying the Earth, and a group of teenagers (are they teenagers?) are trying their be</span>
  <span id="freeText14415262172325415113" style="display:none">Actual Rating: 3.5 stars<br /><br />There are the books that either have too little action and you're bored to tears reading said book, or book that have too much action, and too little of everything else. <i>The Kill Order</i> tends to fall in the latter category of books, and I'll bet that was where Dashner was intending <i>The Kill Order</i> to fall. <br /><br />The plot for <i>The Kill Order</i> is simple - it's the end of the world, sun flares are destroying the Earth, and a group of teenagers (are they teenagers?) are trying their best to survive the apocalypse. Along with the solar flares, men in green suits are coming out of the sky in blimp-like vehicles called Bergs, shooting random people with darts that contain a deadly virus. The group of teenagers try to discover the cure to the virus <s>by doing incredibly stupid things</s> all while trying not to get synched by the solar flares. <br /><br />Now, the execution for <i>The Kill Order</i> is anything but simple (and looking back on the synopsis I wrote, even that doesn't sound too simple). With the above synopsis, Dashner could have had a somewhat simple - but entirely enjoyable - book. While <i>The Kill Order</i> was still enjoyable, Dashner just had to add more to the book. And more. And more. From cults, to ritualistic burnings of people, to governmental deceit, <i>The Kill Order</i> just had too much. <br /><br />With the aforementioned plot points, and much more seemingly random other plot points, you'd expect for there to be non-stop action, right? Well, if you thought that, then you would be correct. A large portion of this book is comprised of thrilling action, and while that might be your perfect cup of tea, it won't be others, and it wasn't mine, exactly. <br /><br />Action isn't the only thing that makes a book a <i>good</i> book. If you don't have enough action, your readers will be bored. If you have too much action, your readers will have whiplash. But, no matter how much action - or lack of it - your book may have, it can't be the only thing going for it. This is the case for <i>The Kill Order</i>. With action, you need to have character and relationship development, especially in a book like this, where the characters are put to the test in an apocalypse. My feelings towards all of the characters in this book were pretty lukewarm - I didn't hate them, I didn't love them, and I didn't like them. They were just... <i>okay</i>... That's not to say that they're unlikable characters, because they're not. It's just that Dashner didn't provide me as a reader with nearly enough character development for me to care for the characters and what they're going through, or to like them.<br /><br />That being said, if you're the type of reader who just wants mindless action after mindless action, pick up <i>The Kill Order</i> - you won't be disappointed in it. The action scenes are very well written and, for the most part, thrilling. However, if you're a reader who values character development in books as opposed to action, <i>The Kill Order</i> won't be the book for you. While I do consider myself the reader who values character development as opposed to action, I found <i>The Kill Order</i> to be a fun, thrilling, and quick read, but sometimes mindless action just isn't enough. <br /><br /><i>You can read this review and others on my blog, <a href="http://findingblissinbooks.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Finding Bliss in Books</a></i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14415262172325415113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2835358458489447659" style="display:none">Well. And let me just say HOLY CRAP. THIS BOOK. I CAN'T. <br />I thought all the other three were good, but this book made me so overwhelmingly....I don't even know. So many feelings. Can I just vent? I'm going to vent, OK?<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ So first...where do I even freaking begin honestly. Alright, let's just start with the end. WHAT. WHAT. WHAT? I honestly was so sad reading the ending. I felt so sorry for them. All of them were going completely insane, and trying to keep it all inside. They hardly even talked at all, and it hit me really hard when I realized that none of them even had the strength to try to help Mark when he fell out the window of the Berg. They were all holding onto their last thread of sanity, and that struggle was honestly pretty hard to read. Even if it didn't outwardly say how he was feeling, their actions spoke louder than their words. When Trina and Mark didn't even talk to each other. OASFOAOSIHFASOIHF OH MY GOSH I JUST REALIZED WHAT THE ENDING MEANT, DUH. SHE REMEMBERED HIS NAME. SHE REMEMBERED HIM. HOLY CRAP, YAY. THAT MAKES ME FEEL A BIT BETTER. <br />What the heck happened to Deedee? I was hoping that the Epilogue would give me some insight into that, but nope. It was about freaking Thomas. I ALREADY KNOW ABOUT THOMAS, I WANT TO KNOW WHAT HAPPENED TO DEEDEE. OH MY GOD. So that was a bit disappointing.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />This book though, I can't even review this like my other ones because I'm filled with so many feelings and questions and angst right now. I haven't stepped away from it and then come back to write this when I'm not all worked up...so this is very raw right now. I literally just finished about ten minutes ago, and I'm still heated and in a completely my-heart-just-sank-what-the-hell-WHY-JAMES-WHY mood right now.<br />Five stars. There. Dear lord, well done. Well done. How do you do this, I don't know. But you are my favorite action author. Favorite author, I'll go all the way for you James. Not like that, I just really like your books. LJA99ad0=a]\[apsfdjlkapsof'jakijw OH MY GOD. I NEED TO CALM DOWN BUT I CAN'T. I NEED TO TALK TO SOMEONE ABOUT THIS. DEAR GOD. I'M NOT GOING TO SLEEP TONIGHT. SERIOUSLY. UGH.<br /><br />I know I should stop writing but I can't.... I'm just so worked up. Can I contact James Dashner? I wish I could have a conversation with the man. Honestly, I need to talk to him. Like, now. GET ME THE CIA, WE HAVE A SERIOUS CASE ON OUR HANDS. THIS BOOK IS A FREAKING, I DON'T EVEN KNOW, IT'S GOT THE FLARE. I FEEL LIKE I HAVE THE FLARE, RIGHT NOW. I HAVE TOTALLY LOST IT. I AM A LUNATIC. FREAKING, I CAN'T. I JUST CAN'T. <br /><br />MAYBE WHEN I CHILL OUT AND HAVE A GOOD SLEEP I WILL COME BACK AND TRY THIS AGAIN TOMORROW. I JUST CAN'T. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2835358458489447659" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_990776312" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/990776312" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/990776312?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=the-earth-is-flat">the-earth-is-flat</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=dragged-on-too-much">dragged-on-too-much</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=boooring">boooring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=dishonor-on-your-cow">dishonor-on-your-cow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=hate-the-characters-hate-the-book">hate-the-characters-hate-the-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=i-should-ve-said-no">i-should-ve-said-no</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer990776312" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8994471893052640827"><b>DNF at 47%</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"Mark jumped to his feet, pulling Alec's arm. The entire area around them shook as it rose, and it took all of Mark's effort not to fall again. He knew that what was happening had to be impossible, and it made him wonder about his mental state."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I know that scene is supposed to have me at the edge of my seat, but the only thing I can think of right now is the lack of cheese sticks in my house, and that makes me wonder about <i>my</i> mental state. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412741154i/11416178.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>After the fuckfest of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7864437.The_Death_Cure__Maze_Runner___3_' title='The Death Cure (Maze Runner, #3) by James Dashner' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Death Cure</a>, I wa</span>
  <span id="freeText8994471893052640827" style="display:none"><b>DNF at 47%</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Mark jumped to his feet, pulling Alec's arm. The entire area around them shook as it rose, and it took all of Mark's effort not to fall again. He knew that what was happening had to be impossible, and it made him wonder about his mental state."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>I know that scene is supposed to have me at the edge of my seat, but the only thing I can think of right now is the lack of cheese sticks in my house, and that makes me wonder about <i>my</i> mental state. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412741154i/11416178.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>After the fuckfest of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7864437.The_Death_Cure__Maze_Runner___3_" title="The Death Cure (Maze Runner, #3) by James Dashner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Death Cure</a>, I wasn't sure I wanted to finish The Kill Order. I'd actually started this before <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7631105.The_Scorch_Trials__Maze_Runner___2_" title="The Scorch Trials (Maze Runner, #2) by James Dashner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Scorch Trials</a> (and experienced the heart-wrenching downward spiral of a promising series) because in a derp moment, I'd mistaken it for the second book. But then, I thought maybe it could shed some light on the crappy world-building. I wanted to find out about the Sun Flares and how the civilization ended. Plus, I'd already started it, so what the hell. How bad could it be?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1412741154ra/11416179.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Apparently, very bad.<br><br>I expected the apocalypse. I expected scenes of the climate growing hotter and hotter by day and baffled weatherman advising people to always wear sunscreen outdoors. I expected scientists running around like headless chickens trying to figure out the problem, while sweating world leaders tried to calm the masses. I expected the inevitable spark to the keg of hysteria, with all hell breaking loose, and people breaking store windows for supplies, acquiring guns to protect said supplies and fleeing to forests where there's more natural shade. I expected a grand mess in the footsteps of the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/149267.The_Stand" title="The Stand by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Stand</a>, or on a smaller scale: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/813214.The_Mist" title="The Mist by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Mist</a>.<br><br>Instead, I get thrown in a world <i>a year</i> after all the excitement has happened. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"We survive months of the sun beating the tar out of the planet, find a place where we can build shelter, find food."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Where is the chaos, I ask you? The murder, the plundering? Where are the religious nuts, like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10592.Carrie" title="Carrie by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Carrie</a>'s mom, that come out and say, "I told you so! Now repent for your sins!" Where are the groups of wild-eyed people in week-old clothes fighting for diapers and tampons? If it were the end of the world, I'd gladly trade my iPhone for a maxi pad. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394766964ra/8903502.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>No proper world-building, no excitement. And I do mean <i>no</i> excitement. We're talking watching-the-paint-dry levels here. Even when the characters were running for their lives, I couldn't work up a speck of emotion to care. The main characters, Mark and Trina, were really bland, like the characters whose names I have already forgotten in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18295852.The_Geography_of_You_and_Me" title="The Geography of You and Me by Jennifer E. Smith" rel="nofollow noopener">The Geography of You and Me</a>. At least I was emotionally invested in Thomas, no matter how much I hated him in the aftermath. Mark and Trina, on the other hand, I care no more for them than I do about the hundreds of tinted food pictures my elementary school acquaintances post on Facebook.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1412510158ra/11384542.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh, wait, I do care about Trina a bit. I care that she, like Teresa and Brenda, are perfect, unblemished specimens of the female sex.<br><br> <blockquote>
  <i>"Man, she was pretty...She turned a page, her green eyes following the words...Her short blonde hair shifted in the wind, and she appeared the very definition of peace and comfort."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Why does every love interest have to be hot? Why can't she have a big nose, or be overweight, or have a weirdly-shaped hairline? I don't like this trend in male love interests in YA and I certainly don't condone the opposite, especially since girls are often objectified in manga and comics. No matter what way you argue it, I highly doubt Wonder Woman wants to fight crime in a cleavage-baring bustier. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1412741154ra/11416180.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Or heels.<br><br>Now I can finally rest in peace, knowing The Maze Runner series is genuinely a one-book wonder. Bland characters, shitty world-building, mediocre writing. Might see the movie, if only for Dylan O'Brien, but other than that, me and this series are done. <br><br>Don't call me, I'll call you. 'K?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1412741154ra/11416181.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/979011657?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of The Maze Runner</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/990726547?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of The Scorch Trials</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/990726570" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of The Death Cure</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8994471893052640827" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_239128851" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/239128851" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6333824-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451437719p2/6333824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/239128851?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/6333824-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6333824-emily?shelf=out-of-this-world">out-of-this-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6333824-emily?shelf=ya-lit">ya-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6333824-emily?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer239128851&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer239128851" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14821635081289905374">ffffff, we have to wait until August? <br/>And yeah, people, this is a prequel. It's before The Maze Runner even took place. I don't know what other people thought, but this trilogy is one of the best I've read and I don't like this genre of book. I am thoroughly looking forward to this book. I do have high expectations for it, and I do think they'll be met. <br/><br/><br/><b>October 5, 2012</b><br/>So, starting to read this, I kind of said to myself "what do Mark and Trina have to do with everything else?" but I gave it a cha</span>
  <span id="freeText14821635081289905374" style="display:none">ffffff, we have to wait until August? <br />And yeah, people, this is a prequel. It's before The Maze Runner even took place. I don't know what other people thought, but this trilogy is one of the best I've read and I don't like this genre of book. I am thoroughly looking forward to this book. I do have high expectations for it, and I do think they'll be met. <br /><br /><br /><b>October 5, 2012</b><br />So, starting to read this, I kind of said to myself "what do Mark and Trina have to do with everything else?" but I gave it a chance because I knew the author had an underlying plan here. So I read it.<br /><br />And it was really effing good. <br /><br />I can only assume that Deedee became Teresa, because of the epilogue. Apparently there's a version with an extra chapter? I'm not sure which that is, so I don't know what went on in it. If Deedee did in fact become Teresa, than it was nice to have this backstory. I liked all these characters a lot - even Misty, Darnell and the Toad. Even though we really didn't get too many glimpses at them, I was sad when they died. But the one character I <i>really</i> liked was Alec. When he had to vaporize Lana, my heart broke. When he flew the Berg away for good, even when he got sick, my heart broke even more. I get these weird emotional attachments to characters and Alec was one of them. And of course, those are the characters that die or something. <br /><br />Anyway, I thought this prequel was great. I want to reread the whole series - they are one series I recommend to anyone and everyone who needs something to read, and this book didn't let me down. <br /><br />Does anyone know if he's writing another one, or was this it? </span>
  <a data-text-id="14821635081289905374" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7243343492341317772"><b>***3 stars***</b><br/><br/>Weeeell, as I suspected.. I did not like this book 👀 But I'm still giving it three stars though, because it was fast paced and non stop action, both things I appreciate in a story. <br/><br/>Right from the beginning, we're told that the story takes place 13 years before the Maze. Except for the prologue and epilogue, where we learn new things about the characters from the original storyline, here we get to know a bunch of new characters.   <span id="freeText7243343492341317772" style="display:none"><b>***3 stars***</b><br /><br />Weeeell, as I suspected.. I did not like this book 👀 But I'm still giving it three stars though, because it was fast paced and non stop action, both things I appreciate in a story. <br /><br />Right from the beginning, we're told that the story takes place 13 years before the Maze. Except for the prologue and epilogue, where we learn new things about the characters from the original storyline, here we get to know a bunch of new characters. They're all survivors of the sun-flares and they're living together in a village somewhere. At some point, trouble ensues and it's only going downhill from there right up to the end.<br /><br />As I said above, there is non stop action going on, so there is barely a dull moment. My problem is that I didn't connect or care about any of these newbies. It was nice learning about how it all began, but I wasn't satisfied with the scientific facts about the flare or the sickness that stems from it. Nothing made much sense to me, it actually felt like just some mumbo jumbo we were told to believe, with little to no real science behind it. <br /><br />The only thing I (barely) cared about was the epilogue. Overall, a very mediocre story.</span>

<div id="review_328408509" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/328408509" />
    <a title="Erika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5666413-erika"><img alt="Erika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361128945p2/5666413.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/328408509?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erika" href="/user/show/5666413-erika">Erika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5666413-erika?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5666413-erika?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5666413-erika?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5666413-erika?shelf=hate-it">hate-it</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer328408509" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18162945904371800112"><b>Before reading the book:</b><br/><br/>Wow, this sounds interesting!<br/>_____________________________________________________________<br/><br/><b>After reading the book:</b><br/><br/>Well, that was disappointing...<br/><br/>I'm gonna warn you guys, and you should take it seriously as a fair warning:<br/><br/><b>Do <u>NOT</u> read this book and/or review if you haven't read the <u>ENTIRE</u> Maze Runner Trilogy.</b><br/><br/>Just don't if you're planning on reading the trilogy. At least not if you don't want to get spoilers for the whole three books.<br/><br/>Now that it's set i will start off by ment</span>
  <span id="freeText18162945904371800112" style="display:none"><b>Before reading the book:</b><br /><br />Wow, this sounds interesting!<br />_____________________________________________________________<br /><br /><b>After reading the book:</b><br /><br />Well, that was disappointing...<br /><br />I'm gonna warn you guys, and you should take it seriously as a fair warning:<br /><br /><b>Do <u>NOT</u> read this book and/or review if you haven't read the <u>ENTIRE</u> Maze Runner Trilogy.</b><br /><br />Just don't if you're planning on reading the trilogy. At least not if you don't want to get spoilers for the whole three books.<br /><br />Now that it's set i will start off by mentioning why this book was such a disappointment for me.<br /><br />After finishing <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7864437.The_Death_Cure__Maze_Runner___3_" title="The Death Cure (Maze Runner, #3) by James Dashner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Death Cure</a>
</i> many people were disappointed with that ending, they said it was all just a waste of time because in the end they couldn't find the damn cure and just decided to go with plan b, which is starting human population from scratch with the inmunes. I didn't think it was that bad, I actually liked it a lot, like it was such a tragic ending, i loved it, but there were things that i wanted to see more.<br /><br />I wanted to see how it came to happen that this people before forming WICKED decided to get such a harsh means of population control, which is the flare, and how it got out of control, and how they decided that making groups of kids go into those trials would help them find the cure.<br /><br />Of course, here it is briefly explained through a few letters how they decided to use that flare virus to kill people so their resources would last more.<br /><br />But I wanted to know more of that, I wanted... I don't know probably more from WICKED* point of view, I wanted to get a better understanding as to why they decided to do everything that way.<br /><br /><i>* Obviously, I'm not talking about WICKED, since it was not yet formed, I'm more exactly talking about the people who later created WICKED.</i><br /><br />Well, I didn't get that...<br /><br />Instead, I just got another survival story with non-stop action coming from characters i just couldn't care about.<br /><br />I hate it how they sometimes made stupid comments or actions just because the author wanted to give the impression that the characters cared about one another.<br /><br />For example, when they took that girl Deedee with them, and the two guys went to where her people went, after spying, the first thing they do is say <i>"Why did you leave Deedee behind? she's just a girl!"</i>. yeah, like they care about her, like it is the smartest thing to do after spying them, and trying to make out if they are insane or not or if they could be of help.<br /><br />It was just very unrealistic, one second one character is caring a lot about another, and the other, they are not even sad the character died. <br /><br />And they are <i>Invincible!!!!</i>. With so much action going on, and the flare eating up their brains plus the sun flares heating them up, I just can't believe how long they could survive <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Only to take Deedee to the Transflat... I had a theory that Deedee was Teresa but it was not explained... hmm...  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />This book just pissed me off. <br /><br />I originally rated it 2 stars, but after writing the review I decided to change it to 1 star.</span>

<div id="review_238487120" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/238487120" />
    <a title="~Tina~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2594672-tina"><img alt="~Tina~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411474324p2/2594672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/238487120?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Tina~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Tina~" href="/user/show/2594672-tina">~Tina~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=netgalley-edelweiss">netgalley-edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=read-2012">read-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=apocalyptic-dystopian">apocalyptic-dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer238487120" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9547547593852788163"><b>The Kill Order</b> is the much anticipated prequel to <i>The Maze Runner</i> series by the incredible James Dashner. <br/>I can't even begin to express how badly I wanted this book. Dashner is one of my all time favorite authors. He's the reason I found my love for post-apocalyptic/dystopic books which provoked me to want to read more in this genre.<br/><br/>This installment takes place thirteen years prior to the initial time setting of the series, which was before Thomas and the Glade, and even before WICKED was create</span>
  <span id="freeText9547547593852788163" style="display:none"><b>The Kill Order</b> is the much anticipated prequel to <i>The Maze Runner</i> series by the incredible James Dashner. <br>I can't even begin to express how badly I wanted this book. Dashner is one of my all time favorite authors. He's the reason I found my love for post-apocalyptic/dystopic books which provoked me to want to read more in this genre.<br><br>This installment takes place thirteen years prior to the initial time setting of the series, which was before Thomas and the Glade, and even before WICKED was created. We follow new characters, Mark and Alec and a group of teenagers battling to survive the aftermath of the Sun Flares. To add more to their already difficult lives, one day a Berg comes out of nowhere and starts shooting darts, killing and effecting everything in its path. <br>The Flare Virus.<br>Mark, Alec and a couple of the remaining survivors hunt down where the Berg came from, to demand answers as to why these people are spreading a virus when the world is already in horrendous devastation. During their journey they see how the virus is affecting people and all the different reactions it causes - from graphic brutalized pain to bizarre hallucinations. Along the way, they do manage to rescue a little girl named Deedee, who miraculously seems to be immune.<br>This is where it all begins...<br><br>Wow! What a prequel! This book is a roller-coaster of non-stop action and heart pounding desperation. I'll admit, I wasn't sure what I was expecting when I found out that a prequel was in the works. I was a bit nervous to read about new characters knowing their inevitable fate. But leave it to Dashner to have me totally consumed by Mark and Alec's journey. Dashner doesn't hold back. This book is filled with thick agony, madness and the twisted minds of unhinged people. I couldn't help feeling so sickened by all the sadness and furious about the unnecessary tactics that caused these people so much grief and despair. A part of me kind of wished that Dashner would have written about Thomas and Teresa or even Newt and Minho. What they meant to WICKED, how they contributed to the plans and life for them before the Glade.<br>The Maze Runner had one constant. Hope. It's what drove the readers to battle it out till the very last book. But for The Kill Order, it felt very fatal, very final. In the end, I'm glad that Dashner decided to share this story. It may feel hopeless, but it wasn't pointless by any means. This is a story for fans who are curious to know why WICKED was born. Why it was good. It's the birth of the Flare Virus and where we learn that certain characters played a vital role in the protection of others.<br><br>Overall, there is no happy ending, but fans of The Maze trilogy already know that, so it’s no surprise. This was a heart breaking and terrifying glimpse into a world that has been utterly destroyed. But it's also a story about fighting for humanity and survival till the bitter end.<br><br>So, with a heavy heart, I'm finally able to let this series go. It's been a fascinating and thrilling adventure. <br>Fans of The Maze Runner trilogy are going to want to experience this prequel because it's a definite gem for their collection!<br><br>I can't wait to see what James Dashner has planned next!<br><br>(Arc provided by Netgalley and Random House Children's Books)<br><br>This review and more can be seen at:<br><br><a href="http://www.winterhavenbooks.blogspot.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333076i/693179.png" alt="winter haven books" width="150" height="111" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="9547547593852788163" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText12364906872004157454" style="display:none">✫✬⭐️ 3/5 STARS ⭐️✭✫<br /><br />Genre: Young Adult&gt;Science Fiction &gt; Dystopia<br />WOW: How the world came to an end. And the ending of the book.<br />EW: The Plot.. really..<br />POV: 3rd-person &gt; Boy <br />ROMANCE: Kinda<br />DO I SHIP IT: Kinda.<br />READ: 2 times.<br /> <br />__________________<br />✎Review:<br /><br />Okay.. there's a thing about this book. This book tells us how the world came as it is in the maze runner. And it was interesting, and really messed up. That i did like. It also really sets up the maze runner. There's one character in book that we know from the first 3 books. And that kinda was a very good plot twist. Also, in the ending of this book, there is a file about Teresa. I really loved that. It's really good. <br /><br />But the plot it self, with the new characters, was not for me. I liked the beginning, but things happen fast. WHY? i would have loved too hang out with them more, maybe let them die trough out the story. Uhg.. And really, i was just.. kinda bored with this book. BECAUSE I WOULD LOVE TO KNOW HER BETTER.<br /><br />Alec:<br />This dude we get to know good. And i loved him. He is just a dad figure. I would want a person like him by my side in this world. <br /><br />Deedee: <br />I loved her having around. Kind a mystery. But also, i would have loved to spent more time with her. <br /><br />-----<br />In General: <br />They die to soon, or they don't stick together, which makes me mad. I didn't had any connection with Mark. And i did with Alec, but we just spend the most time with Mark, Mark alone. <br /> <br />_____________________________<br />❀TV-SHOW OR MOVIE?<br /><br />So the thing is, The director of the Maze runner films said that he was done making films in this world. But Fox still has the rights so the rest of the series, That means also this book. And i do see Fox coming like "And we are gonna make this book into a tv-series" Which i would LOVEEEE. They can change everything. Like for real, and make like 4 seasons. Kinda The walking dead vibe. It would be amazing. <br />_____________________________<br />✧Beste Quotes:<br /><br />“Scared. That’s good. A fine soldier is always scared. Makes you normal. It’s how you respond to it that makes or breaks you.” <br /><br />_____________________________<br />✗Little notes: <br />- Least favorite book in the series. But still good information.<br />_____________________________<br />❖REST OF THE SERIES:<br /><br />✶The Kill Order (The Maze Runner, #0.5) &lt;&lt;<br />✶The Fever Code (The Maze Runner, #0.6) <br />✶The Maze Runner (The Maze Runner, #1) <br />✶The Scorch Trials (The Maze Runner, #2) <br />✶The Death Cure (The Maze Runner, #3) <br /><br />shorts:<br />✶The Maze Runner Files</span>

<div id="review_363267177" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/363267177" />
    <a title="Abby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2262735-abby"><img alt="Abby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565295007p2/2262735.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/363267177?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abby" href="/user/show/2262735-abby">Abby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2262735-abby?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2262735-abby?shelf=abandoned">abandoned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer363267177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14170557031138224231">Also posted here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://wintrywords.blogspot.com/2012/07/arc-review-kill-order-by-james-dashner.html'>http://wintrywords.blogspot.com/2012/...</a><br/><br/>I feel like curling into a little ball and punching a Crank in the face after reading only half of <i>The Kill Order</i>. There’s not much else I can do anymore, feeling like my life is a lie.<br/><br/>I am a huge fan of <i>The Maze Runner</i> series so when I found out there was going to be a prequel I about had a heart-attack. When I somehow manage to land an ARC, I am pretty sure I did indeed die of a heart-attack. My zombie is typing up this review now. The </span>
  <span id="freeText14170557031138224231" style="display:none">Also posted here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://wintrywords.blogspot.com/2012/07/arc-review-kill-order-by-james-dashner.html">http://wintrywords.blogspot.com/2012/...</a><br /><br />I feel like curling into a little ball and punching a Crank in the face after reading only half of <i>The Kill Order</i>. There’s not much else I can do anymore, feeling like my life is a lie.<br /><br />I am a huge fan of <i>The Maze Runner</i> series so when I found out there was going to be a prequel I about had a heart-attack. When I somehow manage to land an ARC, I am pretty sure I did indeed die of a heart-attack. My zombie is typing up this review now. The neighbors probably heard my loud, YES as I read the email. <br /><br />Being disappointed, I will say, plainly sucks.<br /><br />Starting <i>The Kill Order</i> or any book for that matter, I usually plan out the said book elaborately in my head before the description is even out sometimes. I know I shouldn’t, but I think I’m not the only one. Am I? So forgive me, but I thought this novel would be about Teresa and Thomas’s adventure as they created the Maze and more on their family life. I was also majorly looking forward to seeing Newt, Alby, and the others before the Maze.<br /><br /><i>The Kill Order isn’t about any of those things.</i><br /><br />We see a glimpse into that window in the prologue of this story, but it’s blurry at best. And after that the book jumps thirteen years earlier. What is wrong with you, Dashner? Why must you write about something we have no interest in reading? Hmm?<br /><br />I’ll admit I don’t care how the Flare started (you’ve already elaborated) or about how the sun flares scorched the Earth (again, you’ve already elaborated). I want to read about Thomas, Teresa, and the boys honestly, as I said before. The Maze is one of the most curious and complex, yet simply amazing and awe-inspiring structures in all of YA literature and I would love for him to elaborate on that. <br /><br /><i>The Kill Order</i> indeed did disappoint me. It’s all action, action, action. There isn’t much emotion or anything deeper than doing, running, going, jumping, hiding, and dying. In short, it was as dry and boring as a stick in a dead forest.<br /><br />Dashner, I think it’s time to let <i>The Maze Runner</i> series go and write something else. I will probably read it, since Dashner is one of the best writers of YA. But I think going backwards and yet not dealing much with Thomas was a mistake.<br /><br />I am not sure if it was because I’ve read a lot of great books lately or if I have so many I rather read right now more than this. Or maybe some other factor, I am not sure. I mean, every time I tried to read a paragraph my brain was like, "What? You mean you want <i>me</i> to read <i>this</i>?" *laughs evilly* <br /><br />I feel like the whole series was just let down by <i>The Kill Order</i> and with it, my respect and whole-hearted love. Maybe one day when I feel like I should give it another chance, I will, but right now I just feel like putting it down and leaving it alone. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14170557031138224231" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1368306522" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1368306522" />
    <a title="Dannii Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle"><img alt="Dannii Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508499419p2/44487975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1368306522?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dannii Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dannii Elle" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle">Dannii Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781909489431" href="/book/show/22559985-the-kill-order">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=science-fiction-sagacity">science-fiction-sagacity</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1368306522" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18247030171820595701"><b>First Read: January 2015, Rating: 4 Stars<br/>Second Read: October 2018, Rating: 4 Stars</b><br/><br/>This is the first of two prequel novels to The Maze Runner trilogy. Unlike all the other series instalments, this follows a different group of characters and deals with events separate to the WICKED experiments.<br/><br/>The novel opens after the sun flares have ravaged the earth. Those that survived have grouped together in a semblance of a community and an attempt to continue their existence for however and as long as the</span>
  <span id="freeText18247030171820595701" style="display:none"><b>First Read: January 2015, Rating: 4 Stars<br />Second Read: October 2018, Rating: 4 Stars</b><br /><br />This is the first of two prequel novels to The Maze Runner trilogy. Unlike all the other series instalments, this follows a different group of characters and deals with events separate to the WICKED experiments.<br /><br />The novel opens after the sun flares have ravaged the earth. Those that survived have grouped together in a semblance of a community and an attempt to continue their existence for however and as long as they can. But this is not the worst of fates to befall them. As the world is in chaos an organisation is seeking to gain momentum and unleashes a deadly virus that will wipe out or control all that remains of the human race.<br /><br />This book opened up this post-apocalyptic landscape and the reader garners an understanding of how life is lives away from the Glade. Just surviving is still the main objective of the central characters and this makes for very action-dominated reading.<br /><br />I know this is a source of contention with many but I really like how vague this series is on details. I really appreciate how Dashner aligns his characters and his readers in their not knowing. All work together in salvaging whatever clues they can in an attempt to puzzle out the series of catastrophic events that befalls them. This kept me engaged and intrigued throughout, if secretly missing my favourite Gladers a little!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18247030171820595701" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2133363328707795286"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425655747i/13914533.png' width='400' height='300' alt='description/' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>That was a nice ride. actual rating: <b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Mark always loved Trina, even before the world ended. One thing that the sun flares brought together: Mark, Trina. And Mark will do anything to protect her. After their village was attacked and a deadly virus is turning people batshit crazy when it is not killing them is free, the relatively calm life they were living comes to and end and a small group of survivors find themselves on the run again.<br/>Surprisingly, the greatest character by far is Mark's</span>

He steals the spotlights through the whole book and I quickly grew really attached to him.<br>James Dashner has the ability to make every single chapter important in their own way and I love that. Dashner is one of my FAV authors and I wouldn't hesitate in recommending any of his books.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1588696825" />
    <a title="India" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38467984-india"><img alt="India" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476996171p2/38467984.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1588696825?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="India" class="user" itemprop="url" name="India" href="/user/show/38467984-india">India</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38467984-india?shelf=best-book-boyfriends">best-book-boyfriends</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1588696825" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6161653685040348794">Geez, guys, that ending killed me. My book has this extra bit called<br/>"TOP SECRET<br/>Swipe Data Received<br/>Group A<br/>Subject: Teresa"<br/>So, lemme just look into Miss Teresa's (*cough* Deedee) brain here and then I'll get back to you.<br/><br/>Review to come.<br/><br/><br/><b>UPDATED REVIEW:</b><br/><br/>Wow, sorry it took me so long to write this! I wish I could say it was because I needed time to process it or something deep like that, but really, I just didn't feel like it.<br/><br/>Sorry, it's the truth.<br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386615005ra/7403878.gif' width='200' height='130' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Rating:</b><br/><br/>Imma give this 'un here 4.5 flibber flabbin' st</span>
  <span id="freeText6161653685040348794" style="display:none">Geez, guys, that ending killed me. My book has this extra bit called<br>"TOP SECRET<br>Swipe Data Received<br>Group A<br>Subject: Teresa"<br>So, lemme just look into Miss Teresa's (*cough* Deedee) brain here and then I'll get back to you.<br><br>Review to come.<br><br><br><b>UPDATED REVIEW:</b><br><br>Wow, sorry it took me so long to write this! I wish I could say it was because I needed time to process it or something deep like that, but really, I just didn't feel like it.<br><br>Sorry, it's the truth.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386615005ra/7403878.gif" width="200" height="130" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Rating:</b><br><br>Imma give this 'un here 4.5 flibber flabbin' stars.<br><br>I'm sorry, I just imagine Alec talking with a southern accent, and I need to express myself.<br><br><br><br><br><br><b>Plot:</b><br><br>Mark and Trina were alive before any of it happened.<br><br>The sun flares, the radiation, <i>the sickness.</i><br><br>Mark remembers what it was like to just walk home after school. He knows how it felt to be able to trust your neighbors. He knew who his friends were. He knew that he and Trina had each other.<br><br>Now, Mark isn't sure of anything.<br><br>He and Trina were saved by Alec - a former soldier - and Lana - the woman he worked with. With them, they had four other kids. Darnell, The Toad, Misty, and Baxter. They are a tight-knit group working together to survive this cruel new world.<br><br>Mark and Trina are pulled into their lives, witnessing death, famine, illness.<br><br>As the government begins to release a disease meant to reduce the immense population, Mark and his friends are suddenly running from everything. They have nowhere to go, no one to trust but each other. This is their only chance at surviving.<br><br>When they stumble across a young girl named Deedee who was shot with the infected bullet but never got sick, their main goal becomes protecting her. She must be valuable. She is immune.<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><b>Characters:</b><br><br><i>Mark -</i><br>I really, really liked Mark. It was a nice change after reading the rest of this series's books and hating Thomas.<br>Mark was witty, and kind, and so smart. He cared for Trina so much. He was the hopelessly romantic girl that all novels have. Except, he was a guy, and it was great to see him daydreaming of Trina.<br>He may have only gotten the girl because, well, it was the end of the world, but hey! Who's counting that?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392649335ra/8589331.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I know I'm not.<br>I'd date him. He's pretty great.<br><blockquote>“I love the sound of it," Trina whispers, as if speaking too loudly might interrupt the drumming patter of the rain outside. "It makes me want to sleep. Snuggle my head right up in your armpit and snore for three days."<br>"My armpit?" Mark repeats. "Good thing we all showered up in the storm this morning. My pits smell like roses. Go ahead and get comfy.”</blockquote><br><i>Trina:</i><br>I still haven't officially formed an opinion of her. I liked her enough, but she didn't pay attention to Mark until it was almost too late. She didn't realize what a great guy he was until they were all about to die or go crazy or . . . I don't even know. Get burnt to a crisp.<br>They're seriously always in danger. They need a codeword or something.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459384992ra/18604876.gif" width="200" height="90" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Alec:</i><br>The ol' bear. He was my favorite character in this book. He was this big, intimidating ex-soldier, but once Mark got even more close to him, you could really start to see the different sides to him. He was kind but strong and concerned with the safety of his friends. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He was willing to kill the Toad in order to protect everyone else. Even after he did it, he was sniffling and stricken with the guilt of his actions. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>He was super protective of Mark and sacrificed himself multiple times in order to get Mark out of trouble. Given, he always made it out alive. Because he was a soldier. And a pretty good one at that.<br><blockquote>“Okay, listen to me,” the old man said, his voice muffled behind his own swath of fabric. “We need to set some things straight before we get up there. We can’t let our emotions rule everything. No matter what we see, our number one priority has to be saving as many people as possible.”</blockquote><br><blockquote>“Scared. That’s good. A fine soldier is always scared. Makes you normal. It’s how you respond to it that makes or breaks you.”</blockquote><br><br><i>Deedee:</i><br>I KNEW IT.<br><br>There were a lot of other characters, but most of them died, so . . . yeah, we really didn't get to see them much. Honestly, I'm, like, 99% sure that everyone died except for Deedee.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459384992ra/18604877.gif" width="200" height="100" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yes. Every character in this book.<br><br>This government is as corrupt at President Snow.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459384992ra/18604878.gif" width="250" height="130" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><i>Overall:</i><br><br><i>The Kill Order</i> was a great book. The only reason I took away the .5 stars is because the ending is so open. We get to hear about Thomas being taken, but I don't know what happens to Mark and Trina and all them. It ends with Trina and Mark hugging (which gave me ALL the feels, by the way), but we don't know what happens after Deedee goes through the door. To them at least. Because I knew all along what happened to her. . . .<br><br>But they at least deserved an ending. Will they get one?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419355170ra/13044790.gif" width="200" height="100" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380372701ra/726043.gif" width="250" height="120" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'll live.<br><br>Maybe.<br><br>Just waiting for <i>The Fever Code.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459384992ra/18604879.gif" width="250" height="120" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
