<div id="review_1006448121" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1006448121" />
    <a title="Stepheny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny"><img alt="Stepheny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567725280p2/7091879.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1006448121?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stepheny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stepheny" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny">Stepheny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780385742894" href="/book/show/17797357-the-kill-order">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=destroy-it-like-a-horcrux">destroy-it-like-a-horcrux</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=gouge-out-my-eyes-with-a-spoon">gouge-out-my-eyes-with-a-spoon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=why-would-ya">why-would-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=not-even-in-the-zombie-apocalypse">not-even-in-the-zombie-apocalypse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=dystopians">dystopians</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=yawwwwn">yawwwwn</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1006448121" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3233575467189863236">I really wanted so much more from this book. I wanted to know things about the characters that we had been introduced to in the first three books. Instead we are introduced to all new people 13 years prior to the events that take place in books 1-3. All this did was give us a history of what happened, how the world ended, how the virus came to be and how they found out about people being immune. <br/><br/>Through the first three books there are references to Thomas and Theresa's involvement in setting up </span>
  <span id="freeText3233575467189863236" style="display:none">I really wanted so much more from this book. I wanted to know things about the characters that we had been introduced to in the first three books. Instead we are introduced to all new people 13 years prior to the events that take place in books 1-3. All this did was give us a history of what happened, how the world ended, how the virus came to be and how they found out about people being immune. <br /><br />Through the first three books there are references to Thomas and Theresa's involvement in setting up the Maze and how they worked for WICKED. Well, wouldn't you think that the prequel to those stories would involve us getting more insight into what it was that they actaully DID?! That's all I wanted. I longed for character development. Getting to know Thomas and Theresa <i> before</i> the Swipe could have salvaged some of my indifference towards them. But instead the author decides to tell me a story I could really live without. <br /><br />Dashner was strong in the areas of keeping his readers intriged and on the edge of their seats. One area he severely dropped the ball was in the climax. He leads you to believe you are going to have some huge revelation that changes the game and then he pulls the carpet out from under your feet and says "Nope, it really IS that boring story!". I think he could really use some tips in character development as well. I honestly have never cared less about <i>any</i> character in my life. I didn't like a single character in any of these books. Nope, not one.<br /><br />I am so let down by this series in so many ways. I think it really had the potential to be something great. Personally, I think that Dashner just had too many ideas and wanted to put them all in one book rather than developing the top few. These books are kind of all over the place and I won't be recommending them to anyone at any time. Unless I don't like you and want to see you suffer, in which case- here, read this book. ;) <br /><br />What a complete waste of time. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3233575467189863236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/239255984" />
    <a title="Kyle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4506078-kyle"><img alt="Kyle" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/239255984?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kyle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kyle" href="/user/show/4506078-kyle">Kyle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer239255984" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12179320194804573028">Read this review and more over at <a href='http://livingisreading.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'> Living Is Reading! </a><br/><br/>(The gifs actually work on the blog. Have no idea why they didn't work here, but whatever)<br/><br/>Have you ever seen the movie <i> Elephant? </i> I did a few months back. It was just this sort of random indie film that I heard about because I was researching the Columbine massacre, and I heard that the film was based off of that, although it wasn’t about that event exactly. I’d heard very mixed reactions about it, some people saying it was absolute cerebral</span>
  <span id="freeText12179320194804573028" style="display:none">Read this review and more over at <a href="http://livingisreading.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Living Is Reading! </a><br><br>(The gifs actually work on the blog. Have no idea why they didn't work here, but whatever)<br><br>Have you ever seen the movie <i> Elephant? </i> I did a few months back. It was just this sort of random indie film that I heard about because I was researching the Columbine massacre, and I heard that the film was based off of that, although it wasn’t about that event exactly. I’d heard very mixed reactions about it, some people saying it was absolute cerebral brilliance, and others saying it was a cerebral bore. I was fully prepared to love the film and embrace the cerebral brilliance, but then . . . I watched it.<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>Shoddy acting, there was probably ten lines of dialogue the entire eighty minutes, an illogical and unnecessary cliffhanger, absolutely no backstory, too many unnecessary characters that ended up providing nothing for the story, and NOTHING FUCKING HAPPENED.<br><br>I am not kidding you when I say that one of the shooters in the movie played the piano for almost ten minutes straight. AND THEY FILMED AND PLAYED ALL OF IT. At first I thought my Netflix disk was just broken or something, but then I saw that it was intentional. I thought I was going to fucking throw something at the TV, and I was about to go crazy (maybe that was intentional as a sort of metaphor to describe the lunacy of the character . . . hm, maybe I should re-watch it . . . yeah, maybe not). <br><br>TEN FUCKING MINUTES OF PIANO PLAYING. With a twenty second break for two lines of dialogue.<br><br>TEN MINUTES.<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br><i> Elephant </i> is the first three books in <i> The Maze Runner </i> trilogy.<br><br><i> The Kill Order </i> is something that is actually suspenseful and intriguing, fast-paced and completely impossible to put down. <br><br>Now, I am definitely not a fan of the original three books, and this book hasn’t changed my mind in the slightest at the quality of those books. They were terrible shit and a disgrace to the YA science fiction genre, but this is some decent book right here. <br><br>Now, the characters aren’t complex and evocative and multi-dimensional and weren’t what made the book so wonderful. They were merely pawns for this great story that I wanted to keep reading about. The plot basically tells you not only the origin story of WICKED, but the origin story of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Teresa  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I actually didn’t think that this character was actually in the book until I was nearing the last 15% of the book, and I remembered who the prologue was about. <br><br>It is also a story about survival, and the unlimited line that humans are willing to cross in order to survive longer than somebody else. It is the horrifying story of how civilization collapsed in the blink of an eye, and of how it affected not just the world as a whole, but the individual cells of it, the actual people that are now left to cope with it. <br><br>Imagine that when you were seventeen, on the last day of school, on your way home riding the subway through the underground of New York City. Got that image in your mind? Great. Now, imagine your best friend, who is also your secret crush, is sitting alongside you, and life is absolute bliss, completely perfect. <br><br>Then, blink your eyes and suddenly people are dying left and right, and then people are becoming increasingly desperate and violent, and you are forced to flee through the dark tunnels of the subway, and have no knowledge of whether or not your family is okay throughout all this mayhem. Then, imagine that NYC is taken underwater from a <i> massive </i> tsunami just hours later. <br><br>Yeah, I’d have some stuff to tell my therapist too.<br><br>The writing isn’t brilliant, but there is a pretty addictive and readable quality about it that just made the pages fly by, and I was so excited that I just <i> had </i> to know how it would all end and who would live and who would die some terrible death. <br><br>Like I said before, I didn’t particularly love or hate the characters, and felt sort of in the middle for about them, but they definitely drove the story forward in a way that I just needed to know which one of them would kick the bucket next. <br><br>There is some pretty scary shit in this book to, and some images that definitely sent a little shiver down my spine. How the original trilogy is even written by the same author baffles me, since those books evoked absolutely nothing inside of me, except anger and boredom. <br><br>I don’t think this is a sign that James Dashner is going to become one of my favorite authors, or even an author that I’ll end up reasonably enjoying. I think its possible is his Peak Book, but I’m now more than willing to give his next book a try, and see where it goes from there. </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="12179320194804573028" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_459924674" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/459924674" />
    <a title="Jalyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6753938-jalyn"><img alt="Jalyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579800806p2/6753938.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/459924674?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jalyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jalyn" href="/user/show/6753938-jalyn">Jalyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753938-jalyn?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753938-jalyn?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753938-jalyn?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753938-jalyn?shelf=prequels-and-inbetweeners">prequels-and-inbetweeners</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753938-jalyn?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753938-jalyn?shelf=scary-stuff">scary-stuff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753938-jalyn?shelf=will-read-again">will-read-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753938-jalyn?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer459924674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1745492468196930537"><b>Brief summary</b><br/>Before the Maze, before the Scorch, before WICKED was even formed, came the sun flares that changed the world as we know it. Mark and Trina survived what they thought was the worst thing to ever happen to the world, but are now faced with a devastating disease that is ravaging the United States. They, along with some friends, are determined to find the cure that must be out there somewhere and to do that they need to find the people who started it all.<br/><br/><b>What I liked</b><br/>I really wanted to </span>
  <span id="freeText1745492468196930537" style="display:none"><b>Brief summary</b><br />Before the Maze, before the Scorch, before WICKED was even formed, came the sun flares that changed the world as we know it. Mark and Trina survived what they thought was the worst thing to ever happen to the world, but are now faced with a devastating disease that is ravaging the United States. They, along with some friends, are determined to find the cure that must be out there somewhere and to do that they need to find the people who started it all.<br /><br /><b>What I liked</b><br />I really wanted to know what happened in the beginning after the world went to hell in a handbasket and this book definitely gives you that. People can be terrifying when they’re desperate and I felt every emotion that was running through Mark. This book had my heart pounding from beginning to end.<br /><br /><b>What I didn’t like</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Since I’ve already read the first 3 books in this series, I already knew that there was no hope, no future for Mark, Trina, Alec, Lana, the Toad and Misty. That really had me bummed out, but even though it made me really sad, I really think this book contributes to the series. I do wish that we would have been told that DeeDee turned out to be Teresa. I’m assuming that it was her, but I wish I would have known for sure. It would have been nice if the epilogue would have been about WICKED renaming her to Teresa and her meeting Thomas. I didn’t feel it was necessary to have the end be about him. We already knew that part of the story. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Brief thoughts</b><br />I liked finding out how it all began and I would definitely recommend reading this book. I don’t think it would hurt to read this one before The Maze Runner, The Scorch Trials and The Death Cure, but I would recommend reading it last. I liked reading it the way I did.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1745492468196930537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qJn6STml9avj8iC10MeS7Sd+K7RchdmMe21f4us4yAtTMN1rG2FpPiUHJGgm1yhfFHHuuiCBVnxCTcHZagXgsw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('K9IFlFFF9zROZH16YzBL0YBXaqy6YqQ0MLBgkPdyprbQeyK2c4FroYiReaeVIPFjs1ivosZmK8QJkP6rdk+ODg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3857883226429793223">James is the author of THE MAZE RUNNER trilogy and THE 13TH REALITY series. He also published a series (beginning with A DOOR IN THE WOODS) with a small publisher several years ago. He lives and writes in the Rocky Mountains.</span>
